when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實有做些什麼 , 但真正的事情是 , 說未來會比這個要好得多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百多年後 , 這個人出現了alanturing在1936年重新發明了電腦
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是純機械的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但turing告訴我們一些很重要的事情 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學的基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼做電腦 , 都無所謂 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是不是機械的 , 像是babbage的電腦 , 或是電子 , 就像現在的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦一樣 , 或者 , 細胞 , 又或者 , 再一次的 , 機械的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 ,
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它變得很小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 計算的本質
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這就是所謂的教堂論點 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說這東西是babbage建造的 , 其實是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到今天我們用電腦所做的一切 , 只是緩慢而已 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位了解有多慢 , 它的記憶力只有1k左右 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 也就是放進去它的速度比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有一個拉姆派克 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	想要加入大量的額外記憶體
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以有些計劃
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon , 科學博物館的檔案庫 , 有上百個計劃和上千頁的筆記 , 是由charlesbabbage寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組計劃我們稱之為計劃28 , 這也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名稱 , 他是科學博物館裡的電腦策展人 , 也是推動計劃來建造不一樣引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是把它做出來 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有好幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成 。 第二個是對所有計劃進行的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是一個模擬那台機器的電腦最後的部分是把它在科學博物館中做出來
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你不用在你面前弄一個很小的晶片 , 你得要看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽到它 。 我大概聞到了 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們會進行模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫到 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎真的存在 , 它一定會引導未來科學的走向 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從未成功過 , 因為他總是在思考新的計畫 , 但當它真的在1940年代被建立起來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓你們稍微看一下影片裡的動作影片 , 讓大家看一下cpu的運作機制 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪它準備做加法 。 這是加法的運作原理所以你想像這個龐大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代以前 , 我們將會有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個填滿圖像的演講中 , 雅南•阿爾伯特蘭展現了他三項近期的人性調查計畫 , 和我們在他的系列《從上方來的地球》中拍攝的空拍照片 , 來自全球各地的採訪 , 拍攝的影片是《其他六十億人》 , 他很快的演說《家》 , 紀錄了人類對於環境的影響 , 透過呼吸的影片 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannar-husbertrand在寬視範圍內捕捉脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球造成很大的衝擊 , 要飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡是要談談生態學 , 我所排放的二氧化碳和一個法國人一年所排放的二氧化碳量相等 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼辦 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我必須殺一個法國人 , 當我回家時 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵消我的碳 , 比如我每次都這麼做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上我的工作就是展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我會給你們看一些例子 , 最近我在過去一年所拍攝的照片 。

we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油終結

coral reef in new caledonia .	新喀里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	在2050年之前 , 珊瑚中百分之百的珊瑚會因為全球暖化而消失 。

glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。

these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物已經有好幾億年的歷史了 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類能直立步行的歷史則僅有20萬年 。

fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 仍然是人類最重視的職業 。

we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們對於地球的天賦都有同樣的需求 , 希望超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們還是要靠抬高牆維持距離 ,
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰鬥就是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年的時間裡 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 勝過整個人類歷史中 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的流動率很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	集約農耕正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不永續 ,
the climate is changing .	氣候正在變遷 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但貧富差距越來越大
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們正朝著比地球能維持的更快的速度前進 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演說中 , 理查德•瑞斯尼克顯示出將健康照護顛倒過來的便宜和快速基因體排序是如何將健康照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 科技 ,
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	女士們先生們 , 我向你們展示人類基因組
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方則是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男性有一份x染色體 , 當然 , 還有那份小的y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 這只是一個小東西 , 會讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 當然 , 你看到的是雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼被拼出 , 裡面有四個生化字母 , 我們稱之為基對 , 對:a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨便丟出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但實際上 , 如果我把這1280像素點的每一個基對放在800個解析度的螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	可能是因為它的大小 , 順便說一句 , 有著y染色體的人 , 決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以十五年 , 事實上 , 花費了大約四十億美元後 , 基因組排序並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最終的版本發表 , 他們繼續對它的研究 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每基金一塊錢的成本約為一美元這是非常慢的一種方式
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們拿一個基因組 , 大概50份 , 把所有的複製品切割成50基對 , 然後進行大量並行地排序 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	接著 , 我們把它帶入軟體中 , 重新組合 , 告訴你故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看看這個樣子人類基因組計畫:3gb , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一周內有兩百億位元組 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變到六百 。 沒有任何減速的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個基對的價格 , 一個基對排序的價格已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	相當於你在1998年用氣體填充燃料 , 一直等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星及回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口 , 電腦位置 , 所有醫學文獻的存檔 , 摩爾定律 , 古老的定序方式 , 這裡有所有的新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數比例 , 你通常不會看到這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以全球性對人類基因組定序的能力在今年大約是5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們根據被放置的機器知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計將在可預見的未來每年增加一倍、三倍 , 或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一間實驗室 , 佔了所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學院 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人對新的月球絕對是贏家
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學又意味著什麼呢 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人37歲了
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她患有第二階段的雌激素受體陽性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術 , 化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又患上c階段3的卵巢癌
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 ,
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她42歲時再度罹患卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭整整八天後死去
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位婦女接受治療的時間 , 只要不到十年 , 就會看起來像是在放血 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因研究所的研究人員決定看看這個女人的遺體
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他做了定序 , 取了皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 癌症的骨髓定序 , 並在幾週內完成兩組基因組的定序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著他在軟體中比較這兩組基因他發現 , 在其他地方 , 一個2000個鹼基對的基因是tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你有這種基因上的不穩定變異 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒什麼幫助 , 但這對她的家人也有很嚴重的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變基因 , 他們就會得到這個基因測試 , 然後他們會了解 , 然後他們可以去取一般的螢幕 , 及早發現癌症 , 並有可能過著明顯更長的壽命 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我來介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在2歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信這些症狀不符合 , 透過一些英雄的努力和大量的網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有一些其他的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有去除肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀的確改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 這張照片上的那位先生是joebeery , 他很幸運是一家叫做生命科技的公司的執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家製造大量全基因組測序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子做基因測序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一個叫做spr的基因中的一系列突變 , 負責產生血清素 , 和其他的東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給這些孩子使用血清素前導藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	如果沒有全基因組測序 , 這件事永遠不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	當時這是幾年前的事 , 成本是10萬美元 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天的價格是一萬美元 。 下一年是一千美元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	只要是100美元 , 捐贈或花上一年 ,
that's how fast this is moving .	這是以多快的方式移動 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有蝙蝠俠和水槍的小尼克 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果 , 尼克在兒童醫院發現 , 有著這種遙遠的肚子像是饑荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是他沒有吃東西而是當他吃東西時他的腸道基本上會打開排泄物溢出到他的腸道中
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百多次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽媽 , 請祈禱 。 我承受太多痛苦了 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒童科醫師恰巧有臨床遺傳學的背景他完全不知道發生什麼事但他說 " 讓我們把這個孩子的基因組排序好 "
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現一個控制細胞死亡的基因突變
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對於食物的本質有一些免疫反應 , 那是種自然的反應 , 會造成一些編程的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是管控下去的基因卻壞了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這告訴我們有關骨髓移植的治療 , 這是他所接受的骨髓移植 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	九個月後復原 , 他現在在吃沾著a1醬汁的牛排了 。

so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新的玉米、小麥、大豆 , 以及其他能夠容忍乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑的作物 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口我們就得繼續成長和食用基因改造的食物這是我今天要唯一的選擇

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫特展示了他骨髓採取的一種新裝置 , 很快採用拯救生命的骨髓 , 將傷口降到最低 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞 , 可以被用來治療許多條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一個更好的方法來採集骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一個小兒科癌病醫師 , 也是史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床研究專注是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	受到去年ted講者jillboltetaylor的啟發 , 我沒有帶一個人的大腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病患的性命大多數患有較為先進的惡性腫瘤 , 例如白血病、淋巴瘤和其他一些疾病
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植手術 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有鮑勃 , 是一位志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們正在把他的骨髓送到全國各地 , 拯救患有白血病的孩子的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上 , 我們要如何收成這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊看過 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 然後我們拿起這根小針 , 你知道的 , 不會太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們採取的方法是 , 通過軟組織 , 把它打入硬骨頭 , 插入tuchus , 每次用針筒吸取大概十毫升骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她將之放到一個錫罐裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	再把紙交給我 。 我們一次又一次地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約二百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到最後我的手臂酸痛的時候 , 我手上就接到一通電話 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的後端看起來更像這樣 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個手術40年來並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方式 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一種微創的方法 , 一種我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	還有骨髓採取器 , 這裡顯示的方式
our standard seethrough patient .	我們這位 「 看透 」 的病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不是一次性地進入臀部或臀部的後面
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、有動力的導管 , 用一條特別的電線圈 , 固定在骨髓裡 , 然後跟著臀部的輪廓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常迅速的靈感 , 或吸乾 , 豐富的骨髓 , 快速穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過同一個入口
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	然後 , 很快的 , bob可以穿刺一下 , 局部麻醉 , 把它當成門診病人來做 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛拿到了一個小小的補助金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	然後在附近播放這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有了兩隻大型動物還有豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不只得到骨髓的骨髓 , 而且我們還從骨髓採取的骨髓採取了十倍的幹細胞活動 , 和一般設備相比 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年剛被美國食品藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是現場的病人 , 你可以看見它依循著有彈性的曲線變化 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這兒就會有兩次過去 , 在同一個病人 , 同一個人的洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	在局部麻醉下進行 , 作為一個門診病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們在同一個病人身上取得約三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人所做的標準程序還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成體幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還未進入臨床試驗階段 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們身體各處 , 包含在骨髓內的血液改造幹細胞 , 我們採用的是一種幹細胞療法 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	過去十年間 , 利用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病例如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程學甚至神經系統治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛走出來 , 今年我們正在商業化 , 第二代的骨髓採取器 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能幫更多幹細胞出來翻譯成更好的結果
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記 , 成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能使你在更年輕、更健康的情況下 , 可以銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 。 在未來 , 你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終這張照片是我們骨髓移植倖存者的骨髓 , 他們每年都會到史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術可以讓我們未來有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi提出了一個爭議性的新宇宙模型 , 可能只能解答所有的大問題 。 如果沒有其他 , 它是最美麗的基礎粒子和力量的8維模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、技術等 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisi在他所有事情的理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會盡我所能 , 去描述微粒物理的美妙 , 而不用方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 從珊瑚身上我們能學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是一種非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚頭都由成千上萬的珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會不斷地冒出 , 分支出來 , 變成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像一下 , 珊瑚礁是超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們就能單獨挑出其中的一個人 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 他到底是如何在這個特定的位置相較於他的鄰居 , 如果只是機會 , 或著是命運 , 或什麼的 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們調高溫度後 , 他會告訴我們問題很愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以算是相當的 , 你看 , 我衝浪時的疤痕是為了證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這珊瑚繼續跟我們說他鄰居跟他是一模一樣的複製品
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他地點 , 體驗到這些獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支出不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 超聰明的珊瑚將會有獨特的準備 , 來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學──非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實正不斷地分支出不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 將心靈包裹起來是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的奇特現象最早是由薛丁格和他的貓描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個裝置中 , 薛丁格待在一個裝有放射性氣體的盒子中 , 根據量子力學原理 , 將它分支出去 , 讓它進入了一個被放射性的狀態 , 一個沒有放射性的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本散發出去的枝幹中 , 它會啟動釋放毒氣 , 薛丁格必死無疑 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真實被各別的個體所體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	至於兩者都看得出來 , 另一個並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很怪 , 因為我們每個人只會經歷一個獨立的存在 , 而看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每個人 , 像薛丁格一樣 , 是種珊瑚分化成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事情 , 都會發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示所有事情都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理也要描述什麼會發生 , 什麼不會發生 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可歸結到幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡時才會發生的事情 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我用這個來描述我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中質子和反質子的光束被加速到接近光速的速度然後在碰撞中聚合產生一股純能量
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量會立刻轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 使用探測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的歐洲核子研究中心的大型強子對撞機周長17英里 。 當它運作的時候 , 所產生的電力是蒙特雷全市的5倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確的預測哪些粒子會在每次對撞中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都已被實現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必定與質子與反質子相同
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更大的粒子都不會被產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新型粒子加速器如此令人興奮的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將推動這能量極限是以前的七倍之外 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 先讓我描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子粒子的整個動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這個房間裡的很多人都過得很好的生活把他們推來推去
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但是電子還有個中立的夥伴叫做中子不帶電而且是非常小的質量
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下的夸克有很大的質量 , 三者結合在一起 , 形成原子裡面的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些物質粒子分別來到左右 , 各有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有我們不太熟悉的第二代和第三代電量和第一代相同但質量更高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和多種力粒子互相作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子的粒子互相作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	另外還有一種非常微弱的力量叫做弱作用力它只會和左撇子物質相互作用
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克這種強力會帶有不同種類的載荷稱為色載荷而且分別來自三種類型紅綠藍
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪murraygell-mann因為這些名字他們是他的錯
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 通過質量和旋轉與物質相互作用
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都各有不同載荷
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力通過各自粒子所攜帶的載荷和物質相互作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被發現的粒子但我們相當確定存在的就是希格斯粒子它給予所有其他粒子的質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是觀察希格斯粒子我們幾乎確定它會發生
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團在於我們還能看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示這次演講尾聲的美好可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們不同的自旋和載荷計算這些粒子 , 總共有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	很多粒子持續追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然會有好多基本粒子很奇怪
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 會出現一些美麗的圖案 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子擁有一個負電荷而夸克擁有1/3的電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克被結合在一起製造出一個質子時 , 它有一個總電荷 , 再加上一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 帶相反電荷
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷實際上是另外兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這個模式
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做電弱統一模型於1967年組裝起來
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分人只熟悉電荷 , 而不甚了解這兩種原因 , 是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大破壞了電弱型態的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力變弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子在圖中沿著橫向坐標而電磁作用的光子仍然不受質量而且在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被這種粒子載荷的型式在二維空間中呈現出來
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後把載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度空間中畫出來然後投影到二度空間以便我們能觀察到
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子相互作用自然會在這四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞會產生能量四個載荷方向的載荷總量為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都能被創造出來 , 只要它擁有同樣的能量 , 並保持完全的零電荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子 , 這三個粒子還會加入零的總電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持著完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這樣就有了很好的對稱六角形 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強子比如這個強力粒子與有色夸克相互作用比如這個綠色的夸克為夸克提供了紅色載荷
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每個原子裏發生上百萬次使原子核維持一體
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但與三種力相對應的這四種載荷並非故事的終結 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把兩個載荷對應到引力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	把這個加進去之後每個粒子會有兩種不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和旋轉載荷
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都會分開 , 然後在六度載荷空間中給一個不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看出它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個圖案符合我們目前對於大自然的最佳知識 , 在這些基本粒子的微小尺度下建構出來 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們能確定的事 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中是極限的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理了 。 宇宙用這些微小尺度運作的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們還不知道的新舊想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要單靠數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否掌握整個安基拉達 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新的粒子 , 當實驗達到高能階時 , 我們將會看到 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學中有一個舊思維認為這種已知的載荷圖案是不對稱的可以從一個更完美的圖案中出現跟希格斯粒子如何突破電磁圖案來產生電磁效應
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了達成這個目標 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向的新力 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新方向時 , 我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷 , 接著再和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中構建標準載荷集作為更完美的七度載荷空間圖案的一個對稱 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇是1973年由帕蒂和薩拉姆介紹的一個大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎遺失的空隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論運作的方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家將已有的結構作為子集尋找更大更對稱的型態
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案可以讓我們預測那些從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測出了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該和弱力很相似 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷而且考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代有著與第一代物質相同的載荷
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨特的六種載荷
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們在標準載荷空間上彼此坐著 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們就能對每顆粒子分配出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後在八度空間中旋轉看看整體的樣子
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代通過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言小組是個平滑的、彎曲的形狀 , 由248維度組成 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案的每一點都對應到這個極其複雜而美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的彎曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙在最小尺度下的一切運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	在八度載荷空間中生存的這個圖案非常漂亮 , 它總結成千上萬種這些基本粒子之間的可能互動 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到其中包含了許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過某種旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美的物體 , 以任何統一的方式 , 我們可以看到在這個圖案中 , 新粒子需要一些孔洞 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂薩拉姆粒子填補
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置我們知道這些新的粒子應該是疤痕的像希格斯粒子但有顏色的載荷而且和強力相互作用
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著非常深的數學根基 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最漂亮的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的前景 , 這偉大數學美麗的物體能夠描述在最小尺度下粒子互動的真理 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個被數學描述的概念一點也不新 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年伽利略寫道: 「 大自然的宏偉書 , 代表著不斷地向我們敞開的注視 , 以數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何形狀 , 沒有這些形狀 , 人類無法理解它的任何一個字 ; 沒有這些 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中徘徊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾嘗試按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述粒子物理的數學性 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我開始研究這東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但能確保這個數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入到量子力學中 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述為一個不斷成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子會根據美麗的圖案在每個位置互動 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	使用大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器時 , 我們可能可以看出大型強子對撞機是否大自然使用這種e8圖案 , 或是另一種圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新的粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣但對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其它類似的理論都是在拍照時
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道這些想法大多可能最後不會成立於自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多擦擦傷的 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論和新創公司很像 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型投資 , 在失敗時 , 要在情緒上拋棄一排研究 , 就可能很難 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果某樣東西不行 , 你得要丟掉它 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 要維持理智 , 並在這種不確定性中達到快樂的唯一方法 , 就是在生活中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能做到最好去過平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理 , 愛和衝浪中尋找平衡--我的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 即使我所從事的物理研究都沒有成效 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	而我試著在美麗的地方居住
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這對我父母來說 , 這是宇宙中最大的謎題之一 , 我是這樣想的 , 能在那段時間存活下來 , 卻沒有與全職工作有任何相似之處 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我將把你們放在這個秘密上 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色都很相似 , 但在略微不同的地方卻是一樣的 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租讓我把時間花在自己喜歡做的事情上
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	流浪的生活有時是很艱難的 , 但這讓我能活在美麗的地方 , 保持我對於生活的平衡 , 讓我一直都很滿意 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興被邀請來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能理解其中百分之二的部分 , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很傻 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 它之所以能讓少數人至少感到興奮的原因 , 是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它能把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說 , 我們應該想想宇宙 , 最小的事物有可能就是e8的物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 有沒有一個規模 , 以最小的尺度來看 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:我剛剛給你們看的圖案是對應我們所知的基本粒子物理而且它已經和一個非常漂亮的形狀對應了 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的我們肯定知道
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	而那個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似處 , 而它符合e8圖案的方式 , 可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我為你們展示的這些點狀圖案實際上代表著高維物體的對稱性這些圖案在我們所經歷的時空中 , 會扭曲、移動、跳舞
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們看到的所有基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但是弦理論家 , 在我理解它的同時 , 用更小的弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論的震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待e8模型的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動時 , 它扭曲的方向就是我們看到的粒子是什麼 。 所以 , 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 它跟電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:就我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這會是最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都同時展開和發展
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是為什麼我用珊瑚作類比 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	通過這種方式 , e8進入的方式將是一個附在時空中每個點的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時轉折方向就是基本粒子本身
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們將自己呈現為點 , 以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能再講清楚一點 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種驚奇感 , 我肯定想了解更多這種現象 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	非常感謝你們的到來 。 這太棒了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩研究者珍.古德爾談到坦尚尼爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲大鎮和受到威脅的動物並肩生活在一起 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類動物、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	janegooll幫助人類與動物共存
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 隨便什麼 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 嗯 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 !
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	也就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所發出的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽說它從山谷的一側傳到另一側 , 從這一側到下一區 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今晚的演講要接著從昨天zeray離開的地方挑起 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這位了不起的三歲小孩 , selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也曾聽說過透過dna遺傳資料 , 人類的歷史、族譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 已故路易思.李奇 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩之路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在當時那是非常不凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在已經算是常見的狀況了 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石中知道很多關於這些生物的樣子 , 從肌肉的形狀和肌肉吸附作用 , 關於他們如何和他們一起生活的各種工藝品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他認為現在這是個很常見的理論 , 如果我們在現存最接近的遠親大猩猩身上發現行為模式 , 或相同的情況 , 那麼也許這些行為會在七百萬年前出現在類人猿身上 , 像人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們曾從那古老、古老的過去 , 帶給我們的那些特質 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看今天用來處理人類演化的教科書你常發現人們會根據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	他們和我們相似 , 比起其他的生物 , 在這個ted大會中我們也聽過這個故事 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以這對我來說還是要評論黑猩猩在某些方面是如此地與我們相似
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或者她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 。 牠們可以活到六十年或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部份的牠們可能不會在野外活到六十歲
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	wurzel先生 。 母羊十一或十二歲時就生了她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那之後 , 她每五到六年就有一個寶寶 , 在孩童哺育期間 , 有一段很長的童年依賴期 , 晚上和母親同睡 , 騎在背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的孩童對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像對我們來說一樣 , 對學習也是一樣 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物進化時期變得更加複雜所以我們發現學習在個體的生命史中扮演著一個更重要的角色
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩會花很多時間觀察長者會做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 正是如此 , 不同使用工具的行為 , 如今在非洲所有不同黑猩猩族群中所看到的 , 這些行為是如何一代一代地傳下去的 , 通過觀察、模仿和實踐 , 讓我們可以把這些使用工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語的語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 其中有許多是類似的 , 甚至一模一樣的 , 都是在同一個情境中形成的 。 要迎接黑猩猩 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、牽手、拍另一個背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會大搖大擺 , 會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現了很多很多關於同情心、同情心的前導者 , 以及真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 它們和我們一樣 , 有著天性黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們有極度的殘酷 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常有侵略性的行為 , 大部分來說 , 都是針對鄰近的社會群體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常地有侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩們 , 比起其他生物 , 已經幫助我們了解到 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 而且隨著我們做更多的觀察 , 它變得更加的模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始進行的研究至今仍持續到現在 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社會生活的黑猩猩們 , 幫助我們更加了解到 , 我們是其中的一份子 , 並且不分開 , 與我們共享地球的令人驚嘆的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 和世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 發現黑猩猩會失去棲息地 , 蠻可悲的 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 影片中是岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那是我十六年前飛越整個區域時 , 才發現 , 在公園之外的這片森林 , 在1960年時 , 這個森林幾乎沒有裂痕 , 沿著坦尚尼卡湖的東岸 , 那是三十平方公園的地方 , 有一個問題出現在我的腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	" 我們怎麼能試著拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人民正為了生存而苦苦掙扎時 ? "
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地能支援的人更多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	被從蒲隆地湧入的難民人數增加 , 自剛果大湖覆蓋 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	和非常貧窮的人 , 他們在別處買不起食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計劃 , 我們稱之為坦尚尼亞.
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是個很全面的方法 , 來改善住在公園附近村落的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從小在12個村莊開始 , 現在已經24歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入討論 , 但它包含了一些像是樹木的護士 , 耕作最適合這種方法的做法現在降低了 , 幾乎是沙漠般的土地 , 就在這些山區 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方法 , 預防土壤流失
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 使兩年內 , 農地再度能夠發揮生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民們從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的 , 我相信 , 就是和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們微額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	全世界的貸款中 , 大約有95%都回報了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 和教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 這樣她們就能完成中學 , 明確的了解 , 在全世界 , 隨著女性的教育能改善 , 家庭規模也會下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃與愛滋病相關的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的成果 , 是發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	發生在保育上的 , 是這24個村莊的農夫 , 與其視我們為一群白種人來研究一大群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 很多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 那是一個坦尚尼亞人入鄉的團隊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一支坦桑尼亞的隊伍 , 和村民對話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 當山坡的上層都被樹木破壞 , 所以你得到這可怕的土壤流失和土石流 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更大原生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是個遠超出國家公園的範圍 , 延伸到所有這些非常墮落的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地移到一旁 , 所以再一次地 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩們就會擁有走廊 , 藉此他們可以在國家公園外面與其它殘存的團體互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以坦尚尼亞造林計劃是成功的
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們把它複製到非洲的其他地區 , 在其他荒野地區 , 面臨著極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而非洲的問題 , 正如我們前面這幾天在ted的討論中所遇到的 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮問題非常嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量居住的土地 , 並不是那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 將土壤開到侵蝕風化的地方 , 絕望的人口砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能試著為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要捐錢 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他問題不僅是非洲 , 也是其他發展中國家所面臨的 , 甚至是所有我們對地球所做的事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森曾說過如果地球上每個人都有過歐洲或美國人的平均生活水準我們需要三個新的星球
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但是我們沒有這些東西 。 我們已經有了一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡的問題可說是地球上最聰明的生物 , 可以說是有著這非凡的大腦 , 可以用這些ted研討會來說明 , 但是我們卻毀掉了我們唯一的家 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大的決定之前 , 習慣圍坐著 , 問他們自己: 「 這個決定是如何影響我們前面七代人的 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我不是在這裡講到非洲 , 而是世界上任一個已開發國家的重大決定 , 涉及了數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都以 「 這會如何影響下一次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響到非洲
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各處旅行 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林 , 我發現越來越多非洲的問題能夠擺在過去的殖民地開採之門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 到歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 到亞洲去 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我在說的那種 , 我在說污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣經常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源 , 也許是本世紀最關鍵的議題之一 , 不論水到處都是被污染的農業、工業和家庭使用的化學物質 , 它們仍然被散播到全世界 , 似乎都無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯造成的效應更加劇烈 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過了土壤的侵蝕 ,
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有輕率的燃燒石化燃料 , 伴隨著其他溫室氣體 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候出了很大的問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混雜在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是受到更糟影響的窮人 。
it's africa that already is affected .	是非洲已經受影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南的非洲許多地區 , 乾旱的情況更加嚴重 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當下雨真的來了 , 通常會造成洪水和苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在一個無法支援、太貧窮、太貧窮、無法購買食物的地區 , 因為整片土地都被降級了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以當最後一棵樹木被砍掉時 , 沙漠化就變得詭異 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都有
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不驚訝 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到了好多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可能在這個異常聰明的大腦之間有某種不協調的聯繫 , ted科技所證實的那種大腦 , 而人類的心 , 是吧 ? 用非科學的術語來說 , 用愛和同情的觀點來看待這件事 , 是不是有點不協調 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們說話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱的 , 冷漠的 , 痛苦的 , 和憤怒的 。 他們或多或少都說了同樣的話 , 「 我們會這樣想 , 因為我們覺得你已經在消費我們的未來了 , 而我們卻無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經危及了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我就會想我們在他們這個年紀以來如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我會感受到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就引發了我們稱為 " 根與芽 " 的計畫 , 開始於坦尚尼亞這裡 , 現在也擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	這是象徵性的 。 根是堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來似乎很微小 , 為了到達陽光-它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有我們所面臨的問題 , 環保和社會 。 這是個充滿希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人能夠突破這些困擾 , 讓這個世界更美好 , 讓所有生物都能過得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽想傳遞的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人 , 每一天都會造成不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇權 。 在座的每一位 , 我們都能選擇我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人別無選擇 。 這要由我們來改變事物 , 讓貧窮的人也能選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體們 , 都選擇了三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 及哪個國家不論在城市或鄉村 , 都取決於他們在什麼樣的專案計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人 , 開始他們自己的根與芽的團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每個團體都能選擇 , 在他們之間 , 有三種不同的專案計畫 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 認知到這些不同的問題都是相互關聯的 , 並互相衝突 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一個計畫是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會為了幫助世界上其它地方的社區而籌措資金 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物們 , 不只是野生動物 , 家畜類的動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助這個我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	而把這些全部編織起來就是一個訊息 , 就是學習以和平與和諧的方式存在於我們自己、在我們的家庭中、在我們的社區中、在國家之間、在文化之間、在我們與在自然界間共存 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能繼續以我們快要破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們的確不只一個地球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選一個或兩個在非洲的計畫 , 那些根與芽的團體正在進行 , 只有一個或兩個計畫 , 在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果 , 阿拉伯、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說的 , 目前有97個國家在進行 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種樹 , 種有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營中工作 , 有雞和雞在賣雞蛋 , 賺了一點錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽家人 , 讓他們感到自豪和賦權 , 因為他們再也不需要用他們種的蔬菜和雞肉來取得別人的幫助 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	被用在烏干達給予童兵一些心理上的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	進行像這樣的計畫 , 就是讓他們脫離自我 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再說一次 , 他們是社會中很有用的成員
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時間 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽很重要的組成部分 , 年長的小孩會和年輕的孩子對話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不希望懷孕之類的 , 年輕人能更傾聽其他年輕人 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過太多可怕的事 , 你看過你的黑猩猩 , 數量從一百萬隻以上 , 到本世紀末 , 數量不超過十五萬隻 , 數量眾多的動物都如此 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的沙漠
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣沒有希望的會議 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這了不起的人腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想一想這些科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我真的很興奮 , 最後 , 來到人們談著堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往廁所邊沖 , 狀況很糟 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到再生能源亟需
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否為孩子關心地球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否關心他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為全世界精英份子 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做出一些選擇 , 像是我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買些什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	並選擇用這個問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他長大後會如何影響到我孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或其他什麼的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	因此 , 人腦與人心相處 , 我們聯手於世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	而這正是ted的幫助 , 谷歌幫助我們 , 幫助我們 , esri也幫助繪製岡貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在我們把它們連結起來 , 它開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽說過了 。 事情已經開始發生 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這樣的改變 , 這樣的改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們就必須看到這些改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	而下一個原因是希望-大自然有驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個絕對被破壞的區域 , 只要有時間或許可以幫它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子就是坦尚尼亞造林計劃 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我說過 , 這裡看似已死去的樹木殘骸 , 如果你停止砍伐他們來生火 , 這是你不需要的 , 因為你有許多木材 , 而在五年之內 , 你就可以擁有一棵三十英呎的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在絕種的邊緣 , 可以有第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它鼓舞了我 。 它帶到了我最後一類的希望 , 我們在過去兩天中聽到了這麼多的說法:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種由人類決定 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以那些你認為被貧窮、疾病或疾病所打敗的人 , 能夠從中脫身 , 有時只要有人協助他們 , 並且在社會上取得自己的一份子 , 讓他們成為改變世界的一份子 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想那些真正鼓舞人心的人
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一張很長的名單 , 但很明顯的 , 是納爾遜•曼德拉在十七年的辛苦勞工中浮現出來 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著這種不可思議的寬恕 , 讓他可以帶領他的國家遠離種族隔離政權 , 而不用流血打仗 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞他們接手了大型石油公司雖然世界各地的人盡他們最大的努力都被處決了
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此地鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人才是我們需要年輕非洲人的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	而且我們也需要一些環境榜樣 , 我今天也已經聽到了其中的一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以 , 我真的很感激這個機會 , 能再次與ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中的一些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後我要說的是 , 管理這整間會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著證書 , 看起來非常興奮 。 她是根與芽成員 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導下
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這幫她做到她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	這對我來說是非常激動人心的 , 看到年輕人如何被賦予力量的一個例子 , 畢竟有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜.柯恩在海洋中和生活中都有著一些關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 , 和一些關於如何從塑膠垃圾漩渦中解放自己的想法 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍、海洋、塑膠等 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在使用塑膠袋 , 我剪下去 , 縫合起來 , 做成我過去二十年來最主要的創作材料 。
