so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	把這個放在熱盤子上 , 將它設定為溫度 , 只比環境環境稍高一點點你可以看出是怎麼一回事
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這個材料的其中一項原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它可以顯示內容物是否涼了 , 可以喝了 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是眾所皆知的智慧型材料中的一部分 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	再過幾年 , 它們就會成為我們日常生活中使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天汽車但我們可以有能隨著溫度改變顏色的牆壁可以捲起來的鍵盤一關就能變不透明的窗戶
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要來這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對事物的運作方式感到好奇 , 也因為我相信我們應該要對組成我們這個世界的要素有更深的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的複合材料了解得還不夠多 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以取得小量 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	怎麼用它們 , 幾乎找不到可用的資訊 , 對於它們如何產生的資訊卻很少 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以目前為止 , 它們幾乎都存在於貿易機密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業能夠取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年多前 , 我和kirstybole開始進行一項我們稱之為材料公開化的計劃
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是一個我們和任何其他想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發佈資訊、鼓勵他人盡其所能 , 並且聚集資源 , 像是其他像我們一樣的自造者的研究論文及課程 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個由許多智慧型材料自行生成的大型資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但是為何我們應該關心智慧型材料的運作方式和組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解、不使用的東西 , 最終塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 穿的衣服住的房子 , 都對我們的行為健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們生活在一個以智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要了解、了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 也同樣重要 , 創新一直都是由 " 修行者 " 推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 而非專家們 , 一直都是發明家和改良者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機等 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰在於材料科學很複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但也不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩位科學家就這樣理解了 , 當時他們發表了一篇論文 , 用較簡單的方法製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登邦克 , 在那之前 , 他完全沒有任何化學經驗 , 讀過這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間進行實驗 , 只使用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據另一位科學家的說明書自製的旋渦混音器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來在網路上公佈了他的研究結果 , 包括他所有嘗試過且沒有用途的事情 , 讓其他人可以去研究、重現它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬登創新的主要形式是把在大學設備精良的實驗室所創造的實驗放到芝加哥的車庫裡只使用便宜的材料和工具他就自己做出來了
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這份工作 , 其他人可以挑出他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的流程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個我想要提到的例子 , 她的計畫目標是要強調材料的表現特質 , 同時要聚焦在建造者的創造力和技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備的功能非常強大 , 能教導我們事物運作的方式 , 但設計上的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的做法 , 另一方面 , 是要制定一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 透過教導我們認識材料本身 , 來解放我們的限制 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅線 , 連到mp3和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜用各式各樣的材料做出一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布和油墨 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登以及許多其它的製作者漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 允許任何人複製和繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但是紙電子是最有前景的材料科學其中一個分支讓我們能創造出較便宜且有彈性的電子產品
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝成果 , 以及她分享她的發現的事實 , 開啟了一系列新的可能性 , 既有美感又有創新的可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們從熱情和好奇心所創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從非傳統的角度解決問題 , 並且 , 在過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人在材料上做實驗 , 越多研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 我們就有更好的機會創造出能服務所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得像泰德尼爾森一樣 , 在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 現在你一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	在那時 , 電腦是只有科學家在乎的大型主機 , 沒有人夢想能在家中裝一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	別忘了 , 要取得關於新興科技的先見知識 , 是確保我們在創造未來時能夠發表言論的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖門然後按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面的少數幾輛車 。 但如果車子能互相分享彼此的位置和速度 , 並使用預測模型 , 來計算每個人在道路上的安全路線呢 ? 珍妮佛.喜:想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛:如果車子能說話 , 意外事故可能會被避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去想的事情之一 , 但事實上 , 宗教代表以及好運的魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 都背叛了我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而其中75%的車禍和毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上當時還是個年輕的司機前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我想: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這個人在放慢速度 , 我也會放慢速度 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這個傢伙沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人正在停車 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛好是65比0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我輕敲剎車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感到abs啟動了 , 車子依然啟動了 , 它也不會停了 , 我知道它不會停了 , 空氣袋子已經裝完了 , 車子完全沒有被傷害 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停了我想我們可以做得更好
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以轉變駕駛經驗 , 藉由讓我們的車子彼此對話的方式 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想請大家想一想現在駕駛的體驗是什麼樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車 , 關上門 , 你在一個玻璃泡裡
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受你周圍的世界
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的軀殼裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是在看不見的道路上行駛 , 和其他巨型金屬巨型巨型生物之間 , 以超人類的速度行駛 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	懂嗎 ? 你只需要指引你兩個眼睛
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 這就是你所有的眼睛 , 眼睛雖然不是設計來的 , 但後來卻有人要你做像是 , 你想做條車道的改變 , 他們要你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼光從路上移下來 , 沒錯
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看向你要往哪裡去 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後在路上開車 , 不去看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全駕駛 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這麼做 ? 因為我們必須做個選擇 , 看這裡還是我看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上要走的路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯失什麼 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會意識到做錯了或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 駕駛們說: 「 我沒看到它來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	而我相信 , 我相信這點
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得見這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技的確存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這個狀況 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了車輛互相交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到前面三輛車以及三輛車的後面三輛 , 右邊和左邊這一切 , 同一時間 , 鳥的視線 , 我們將能看到那些車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將可以看出前面車輛的速度 , 看出車子的速度有多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要下降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預知模型 , 我們將能夠預知未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你們可能認為這不可能
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你怎麼能預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 。 有車子的是 , 這不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿路行駛
often they travel on prepublished routes .	經常在預先發佈的路線上行駛 ,
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來位置並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車上而有一些機車騎士來到你的車上 , 每小時85英里的路程我知道你曾有過這樣的經驗 「 無中生有 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙可能在前半小時路上
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里前 , 有人看過那傢伙 , 一旦有一部車看到那個人 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上的位置、速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那另一輛車會在他的耳邊低語一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我是說 , 它們是牛頓式的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	對他們來說那是非常棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達成 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的事情開始 , 分享我們車子間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車子裝有gps和攝影機 , 我就會知道我在哪裡 , 以及我多快要走 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	藉由電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車在哪裡 , 算是去哪裡 , 以及他們要去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們能精確的知道自己身在何方也能想出其他車子在哪裡
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車子共用那些資料 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會怎麼樣 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 模擬出了當毛茸茸的估計加上流量 , 甚至是輕型車流 , 當車子只是共用gps資料時 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬移出 , 移到裝有感應器的機器床上 , 裝在這些機器人身上:音響相機、gps、gps , 以及二維雷射雷射雷射測距儀 , 這些都是共通的備用系統 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的無線電機台 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器在互相靠近時 , 它們可以精準地追蹤到彼此的位置 , 它們可以避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	有個問題 , 當你的聊天太大時 , 就很難去處理所有的包裝 , 所以你得要優先處理 , 而那是預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤那些預期的軌跡 , 你不會太注意那些資訊封包 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離航道的傢伙列為優先 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以推斷出新的軌道
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道了還知道他要怎麼偏
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪個駕駛需要警告 , 才能離開路面 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要做到最好警告所有人的行為嗎 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲警告: 「 你得趕緊離開 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在打電話 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能沒有在緊急狀態中做出最佳的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了不同的研究 , 做一些駕駛狀態的模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三台攝影機的一系列攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛人是否有在看前面、在電話中 , 或在喝杯咖啡時 , 來偵測 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們能預測意外 , 並且能預測是誰 , 哪一輛車 , 最好的位置是要走出去 , 為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	根本上 , 現今的這些技術
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是個很讓人不安的想法 , 認為我們的車會在看著我們 , 和其他車聊天 , 說我們會在一條流言的大海中沿著道路走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信這可以用一種保護我們隱私的方式來完成 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我看著你的車子從外面看 , 我不知道你是怎麼一回事 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的牌照號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以談論我們背後的我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們考慮一下如果你真的不希望那些分心的青少年在你身後知道你在煞車知道你要停下來
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到對每個人最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車去聊你吧 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	能使道路使用更為安全
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現他前往太空的夢想 , 通過飛向上空 , 一起飛到大氣層 , 體驗到無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、太空、科技、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdiamandis在stephenhawking在g0henhawking的stephenhawking
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我熱衷於打開太空前線 ,
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	而我想要告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 透過基因體學archonxprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 將十天內第一個完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因體-100人組-這是我們進行基因體定序的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力狀態 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他當場就說: 「 絕對可以 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 在地球上 , 要體驗無重力飛行 , 唯一的辦法其實是要搭乘拋物線飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛到頂端 , 飛了25秒都無重力 ,
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 體重就會增加兩倍
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以有八到十分鐘的無重力經驗nasa如何訓練太空人這麼久
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們就宣布要飛史蒂芬•霍金
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	有一家政府部門和一家公司經營者說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你們會殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們召開了記者會 , 我們宣布了我們的目標要做一個無重力拋物線飛行 , 給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切非常順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他想上去做這個 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生物面臨著不斷增加的危機 , 被災難所消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不上太空 , 就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對於太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他去甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車子裡 , 進入zero-g飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個捐款的人--我們為兒童慈善團體募集了15萬美元的捐款 。 他們和我們一起飛去 。
a few tedsters here .	幾位tedsters在這裡
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士 , 登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們正在監測他的二氧化碳他的血液、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一緊急事件發生時 , 天知道 , 你並不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 在那裡 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我和我的夥伴byronlichtenberg小心地將他吊進0格 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的真正樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	經過第一個拋物線飛行之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說開始 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實讓一顆蘋果漂浮在艾薩克.牛頓爵士上 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋拿著和艾薩克.牛頓相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、第五和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這位男子看起來不像65歲輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 正是在我們有生之年 , 我們正在離這個星球而去的 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請與我們一同參加這趟史詩般的冒險之旅 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫師大衛•布林斯基有3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 呈現出在細胞裡面的繁忙生活 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計 , 娛樂 , 電影 , 健康 , 醫學 , 科學 , 科技 , 視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky將細胞的活化
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一個醫學繪圖師 , 我從一個稍微不同的角度
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在觀察 , 自從我長大以來 , 藝術中真與美的表現方式、科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己所擁有的美好事物 , 他們都有非常美好的東西 , 為他們帶來真與美 , 作為理想的事物 , 可以被科學或是數學所檢視 , 幾乎就像是理想的連體雙胞胎 , 科學家會想要與他們約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是 「 真 」 的表現 , 真象是令人敬佩的事 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 , 不可思議 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是有用的 , 通常在事實之後很長一段時間之後 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你真的可以在上面滾動一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美 , 對科學不在的人來說 , 往往是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們所描述的 「 美 」 的方式 , 通常只有你懂得該主題的人的語言和語調 , 才能夠懂得該主題的真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡存在一個人類學的理想 , 你會發現生命從描述宇宙的數量來演化出來--這些都是非常難理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我接受醫學插圖的訓練後 , 我試圖去做的是--從我被父親教導動畫 , 他是一個雕塑家和視覺導師我想要想辦法幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 通過動畫 , 通過運用圖片 , 說故事 , 讓那些不見得能被人們所接受 , 並且能夠被傳授 , 並且能夠被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常都沉浸在一種環境中 , 在那裡 , 他們所學的就是有真與美的主題 , 但教導他們的方式是分離的 , 吸引的就是真與美並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的老食譜 , 你讓雞肉沸騰 , 直到香味通散去 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們才有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話 。 他問我我和我的團隊 , 是否有興趣而且有意願改變哈佛的醫學與科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們開始了一項探索細胞的計畫 , 探究分子與細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 讓學生能夠了解這些事實的更大圖片 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能會有一個對於細胞的心理印象 , 一個巨大、繁忙、非常複雜的城市 , 被微型機器給佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 能讓世界各地的奈米科技很嫉妒 , 它們是能自我引導、功能強大且精準的裝置 , 用一串胺基酸做成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能驅動細胞的移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞複製、驅動我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想要做的是 , 找出一個動畫 , 讓這個故事成為哈佛大學biovisions的中心 , 它是一個哈佛大學為分子與細胞生物學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有的文字資訊外 , 所有教學內容以外 , 讓這些學生能夠以視覺呈現 , 將細胞內部的真與美呈現出來 , 並且能夠用這個觀點來研究 , 因此 , 將他們的想像力發揮出來 , 發揮出來 , 發掘出生命力 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們從觀察這些分子是如何結合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們的研究主題是 , 你有巨噬細胞 , 它們會沿著微血管流動 , 它們會觸及微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁上搜尋訊息 , 它們會得到外面某處有發炎的資訊 , 在那裡 , 它們會看不見也感覺得到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但它們得到讓它們停下來的資訊 , 讓它們能夠內化到需要製造出所有會造成它們改變形狀的各個部分 , 試著從這個微血管中走出來並找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家合作 , 與資料庫模型 , 準確無誤的原子分子 , 找出它們是如何移動 , 然後弄清楚它們是怎麼辦到的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出辦法 , 用真誠的方式 , 來解釋到底發生了什麼事 , 但不說實話 , 細胞中那些緊密的擁擠 , 以避免視線發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我現在要播放的是我們所製作的這部影片的第一層部份的 「 三分鐘閱讀器 」 版 。 這是一個持續進行的計劃再過四到五年
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們能看到這些 , 看到細胞製造這些會走路的小機械 , 它們叫做動能蛋白質 , 用這些巨大的負荷 , 來挑戰相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很神奇 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都會相互作用 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞信息 ,
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們導致細胞內不同的事情發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會利用能讀取基因的分子 , 來製造果蠅需要的部分 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 若沒有這些小微機械 , 將不可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , chris , 真的非常零散 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex快遞小弟 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他拉起了一個全新的製造蛋白質到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜 , 不論是對一個器官而言 , 不論是用來製造或修復一些東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西正在你的一百兆個細胞內運行 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上你並不是在做什麼都沒有 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家後能想想這一點 , 並想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並思考一些我們正在學習的關於細胞機械學的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們明白了所有正在發生的 , 相信我 , 我們知道幾乎百分之一發生了什麼 , 一旦我們了解發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠掌握我們對健康的掌控權 , 用我們對未來世代的做法 , 及我們要活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能利用這個發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們知道細胞需要什麼來支撐它們 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們會一起運作 。 它們讓細胞做它該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們同心協力 , 協助我們的身體龐大 , 它們永遠無法看到正常的運作 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	請享受接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪布蘭頓打算在車上住一整年 , 看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症進入時 , 她的自由工作結束 , 她的露營旅程就變成無家可歸 。 在這場親密的演說中 , 她描述了她成為其中一名在工作的無家可歸者的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:那一年我無家可歸的日子
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是非常好奇的人 , 所以 , 身為記者的我 , 已經學會了很多新事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學會的其中一件事就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了在職無家者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後我決定去旅行
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我受到很大的打擊 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當時我在做這件事時 , 有很多事想感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 我決定在旅行車中住一年 , 就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	於是我打包好我的貓、我的旋轉木工和露營裝備 , 裝上1975年雪佛蘭小貨車 , 開車去日落 , 完全沒有想到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會將永久的結構分類 , 甚至一塊小屋 , 擁有個人價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 別人的負面看法會影響我們的現實 , 只要我們願意 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	剛開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 。 我經常吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我還有時間可以放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親去世時的憤怒和沮喪 ,
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的 「 自由工作 」 結束了 。 而我必須找全職來支付這些帳單
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天整個溫度轉變為冷酷無情的夏天
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 都不可能停車 , 而不明顯地我有隻貓和一隻狗 , 且那裡真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓咪來了通過箱型車的開放窗戶
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗送進 「 生日照護 」
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	任何時候 , 我都用辦公大樓的員工淋浴間和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室洗的
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人幾乎無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在高溫下腐壞
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰粒 , 幾小時之內就融化了 , 實在令人相當痛苦 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我買不起公寓 , 或根本負擔不起一間公寓 , 讓我能夠擁有rotweiler和cat 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當這些熱氣讓我連去走50呎到晚上在我車外的公共廁所時 , 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度下降到零度以下 , 持續在那兒
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一整套新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每晚都把不同的地方停下來 , 這樣我才能避免被警察注意到和抓到 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不是一直都能成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得無法掌控自己的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我也不知道何時或如何發生但我從一個才華橫溢的作家和記者變成了一名住在旅行車中的無家可歸的女性把我的呼吸帶走
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒變 。 我的智商沒變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、正直、價值觀、一切關於我的一切都還是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我卻以某種方式改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪中越加深入 ,
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	終於有人把我轉診到無家可歸的健康門診 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中任何人一樣臭、一樣沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或高不喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數名流浪漢領悟到 , 包括前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不無家可歸 , 你為什麼來這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不把我當成無家者 , 但我知道了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的抗憂鬱症讓我有自殺傾向 , 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有一個朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 在全國各地都在談我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他去世前的那一年 , 就在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	當時他在演說節目電路裡 , 提到我的寫作
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我了解到timrussert , 《與傳媒會見》的前任主持人 , 正談論著我的寫作 , 當我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了因為它達到了我是作家還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀了我的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後我搬回了田納西 ,
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我在住在旅行車和朋友的沙發上做個交易 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天我是一名工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再被忽視 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職、兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化 , 並將住在你車上或街上犯罪化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 職業的無家者 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一個 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服一切只要有希望
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當海報女孩無家可歸 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們捐錢給你們遇到的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是生活的地方 , 他們睡哪裡 , 也不是他們的人生狀況如何 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在旅行車上停在沃瑪超市的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 永遠要找到出路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 " 保險套先生 " mechaiviravaida , 帶我們走過這個國家的大膽計畫 , 提高生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 有趣的 , 和非常有效的關於安全套的演講 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaida:保險套先生是如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有非常多的人民生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 也不是從貧窮減輕計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	我們從一個家庭計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 組成許多活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受如果他們的孩子沒有生存下來 ,
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:先到孩子那裡 , 去找母親們 , 然後再接著做節育計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的狀況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭平均有7個孩子有極大的成長率有3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 就去做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們也同意 , 我們會使用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 而我們只有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 一 」 看作答案 ; 我們把 「 一 」 看做一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找了護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸上 , 做了一個很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很美好 , 但它只佔了全國20%的面積 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為另外的百分之八十的人做了什麼 ? 然後說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們就去看你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那個黃色標誌下面 , 我希望他們還沒看到那個 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那時候我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的對象 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中相當知名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們非常的棒 , 他們自己執行節育計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應避孕藥和保險套到整個國家的每個村落 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們在那裡 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的起因的人 , 成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論人在哪裡 , 你都能看到船上的女人 , 賣東西這裡是漂浮的市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找人 , 你都會發現避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為何不宗教呢 ? 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會相當堅強 , 泰國人都是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 聽著 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那兒 , 藍色的不是黃色的 , 手上拿著一碗聖水給僧侶 , 讓僧侶在避孕藥和保險套上撒下神聖的水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳到全國各地
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶也自行做同樣的事情 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	婦女們說: " 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們找了教師
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人參與 , 試圖提供任何能讓人類變得更好的東西 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師們
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人教導了節育計畫 , 用新的字母a、b、b、c、保險套、i、v、輸精管切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了一條蛇和梯子遊戲 , 就是把骰子丟在那裡 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何明顯計畫上著陸 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是 「 媽媽每晚服藥 ,
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 。 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	舅舅會買保險套 。 很好 , 舅舅 。 往前走 。

and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久前 , 保險套就知道是女孩子最好的朋友了 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮苦人家來說 , 鑽石不把它做出來 , 所以保險套就是女孩的好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進微型貸款計畫 , 負責這項計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想借給有執行節育計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 就照顧自己的懷孕吧 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	而那是由他們經營的
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36年仍然持續著
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村莊發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 而是一筆基金 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個龐大的組織來運作 , 由村民自己操作 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能很難在那看到泰國男人 , 總是有女人、女人 。

and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是在七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定要為全體男性提供輸精管切除術 , 但特別是 , 排在隊伍最前面的美國男性 , 在他[不清楚]期間 , 接近大使的住院 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館給了我們球場 , 非常貼切的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然已經快到了午餐時間了 , 他們就說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 那一定是美國的可樂 。

and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物要嘛是漢堡要麼是熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得熱狗比較有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這是一位名叫威利•鮑姆的年輕人 , 他為美國國際開發總署工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯的 , 他已經做完手術了 , 因為他的熱狗吃了一半 , 他非常開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	在美國引發了許多新聞 , 也讓某些人感到憤怒
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 。 來吧 , 我會為你們所有人 。 」

you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂法 , 只要你喜歡它是完全相同的東西 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不太確定可口可樂是不是跟著我們 , 還是跟隨著可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的例子 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強勢的政府 。 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但是每一個人的工作都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病襲擊泰國 , 我們不得不停止對抗愛滋病 ,

they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	擁有的比政府多 , 擁有的槍也比政府多 。

every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每一個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都必須接受愛滋病的教育--每一個人 , 我們都說大眾、機構、宗教機構、學校--所有人都參與 。

and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	而這些是高中生教授高中生

these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級的孩子 , 去村子裡的每戶人家 , 整個泰國的每戶人家 , 都在使用輔助資訊和保險套 , 每個家庭都是由這些孩子提供的 。

so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以 , 你可以看到 , 我們在努力的過程中加入了一切 , 讓人們的生活更加美好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們把保險套放在旅館和學校的所有冰箱裡 , 因為酒精很容易判斷 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助大家脫離貧窮 , 現在我們已經得到艾滋病──這次不是只有政府 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 也無法取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些被商業界提供的東西
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳的企業家 , 小生意人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業
so , that was done .	這樣就完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	經費由公司流入村莊--用樹木移植
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種樹 , 錢就到他們的小額貸款基金中 , 我們稱它為村落開發銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧困中的人 , 信用能力必定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用能力必須要成為一種人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離不了貧困 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你必須接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這裡我們稱之為赤腳企管碩士班 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 如此一來 , 等他們借到錢後 , 他們就會成功地做生意 。

they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	讓這些變得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以任何坐著看電視的人 , 要和我聯絡 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	最後 , 在教育上 , 我們希望改變學校的教育 , 把學校當作沒被使用的地方 , 讓每個人都成為了一生的學習中心 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為學校的整合式郊區發展
