he was quite a figure .	他是個很像的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他後來成為印第安那瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生發表公眾講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡告訴各位 , 如果有任何事比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 那就是試著要在45分鐘的演講內掌握1000個12歲孩童的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	講座結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個自此之後深印我腦海中 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想 , 有些人認為偉大的地球探索時代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將不得不前往外太空或最深的海洋 , 去尋找一些重要的值得探險的東西 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有重大的意義嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未被看見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始要找出菸草鑲嵌病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的是取出菸草屬植物的受感染汁液 , 經過愈來愈小的過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	到達那時 , 他覺得一定有什麼比當時認知的最小型態的生命形式還要更小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人取了個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之病毒為拉丁文的 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , 實際上beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道 , 病毒構成地球上大多數的基因信息 , 比起所有其他形式的生命體的基因信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然已經有大量的實務應用和這個世界有關係--像是天花的消滅 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 現在我們知道大部分是由人類乳頭瘤病毒所引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的事情
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	在至少一百年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們有汽車 , 但是我們不知道構成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具可以讓我們探索未知的世界--比如深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得更多 , 不僅僅是瀏覽及特定物種的個別基因組 , 還可以觀察整個微生物群落 , 在我們周圍、在我們周圍 , 並記錄這些物種中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚間的所有物體上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在經常這樣做 , 確切地確認造成疫情爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	先讓各位了解一下這是如何運作的 , 想像我們取了你們每個人的鼻腔線條 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們常用這個方法尋找呼吸道融合病毒 , 像是流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到一些人類的基因信息 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒資訊 , 大多來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了令人非常吃驚的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊 , 我們會發現 , 你的鼻腔中大約有20%的基因信息不符合任何我們從未見過的植物、動物、菌類、病毒或細菌的基因信息 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際在研究這類資料的小組而言 , 有些人開始稱這個資訊為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何以前我們見過的東西 , 它有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之二十的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的信息是暗物質是無法被歸類、無法與我們以前看過的任何東西配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為也許這是人工製品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這信息是一種生命的形式 , 至少其中有一部分是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設都還在初步階段 , 但仍然有一種非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那就是埋藏在生命裡的這個遺傳信息中 , 是尚未被辨識出生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c和g時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命類型 , 就像beijerinck一樣 , 將會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的認知 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那也許能讓我們找出折磨我們癌症的原因 , 或是找出我們不熟悉的爆發病源頭 , 或也許能創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 加上史丹佛大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們 , 正在開展一個計畫 , 來探索生物暗物質的存在 , 來探索新的生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們沒有意識到病毒 , 這種生命形式組成了我們星球上大部分的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能驚訝於我們可能完全沒有意識到我們眼前的新生命階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能也發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同事為下一代的探險家提供了重要的教訓像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們說這一課 , 可以說是這樣的:不要假設我們現在認為存在的就是整個故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追尋任何你選擇探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周圍有未知 , 只等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇性的科學家大衛.狄克斯奇把理論物理放到火葬上 , 來討論更急迫的物質:我們人類的生存 。 邁向解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要去肢體上 , 說些意外的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	而事實上 , 第一件是從有史以來就知道的事 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其他 , 都獨一無二的適合維持我們的演化或創造 , 如同以前的思想及我們現在的存在 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	太空船之外的想法 , 宇宙之中充滿了敵意 , 而其內部是我們所依賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸了太空船 , 沒其他地方可去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 第二件大家都知道的事是與人類歷史中大部份時間所堅信的相反人類事實上並不是存在的中心
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬霍金有句名言所說 , 我們只是存在於典型行星表面的一種化學污垢 , 圍繞著一個典型的恆星運轉 , 位在一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的兩件事當中的第一項好像是在說我們身處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合之類的 。 第二件事是說我們處在一個很典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是你認為這兩者是深層的真理 , 能依此生存並傳遞你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎有點互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不會讓他們兩者都完全虛假 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 是一個典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們來看看隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 和一個化學污垢 , 這一點也不典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是往同樣的方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你完全看不到任何牆面或化學污垢--你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那對宇宙來說仍然不算典型因為恆星存在於星系中
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 離任何星系還差得很遠 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以讓我們走出去 , 直到我們走出星系 , 然後再回頭看 , 是的 , 那裡有著巨大的星系 , 螺旋形的手臂 , 呈現在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	這時候我們已經來到十萬光年了
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然離宇宙中一個典型的地方很近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須走到一千倍到達星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那又是甚麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在極大的代價下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的沉浸式虛擬實境 , 將星系間空間的視野給呈現出來 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 讓大家看一下嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美--你看 , 在星系間的空間是黑暗的 , 漆黑一片 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正盯著離你最近的恆星 , 而那顆恆星正好是超新星爆炸 , 而你正直直直地盯著它看 , 在它的光線到達你眼前 , 你仍無法看到任何一絲的閃光 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是如此之大和黑暗
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管一個超新星如此的明亮 , 這麼傑出的一個事件 , 以至於它會在數光年時把你用石頭砸死 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你根本不會看到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷不超過絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且空無一物 。 那裡的真空密度比地球上最高的真空狀態還要低一百萬倍 。 這就是我們在這個地方不同的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	那就是這個地方有多麼不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈開亮點嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何得知一個如此遙遠、如此不同、如此遙遠的環境呢 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這是什麼意思呢 ? 比我們剛才所指的還要遠 , 以望遠鏡看 , 然後你會看到類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為類星體 。 類星體原本的意思是類隔物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看上去有點像星星的東西 。 但它們不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 幾十億年前 , 離我們有數十億光年之遙 , 在星系中心的物質朝著超大質量黑洞塌縮 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後密集的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用.其中一些物質以極大的噴射流束的形式退出 , 以光亮的角度呈現 , 我認為是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理現象和噴射流的物理相比 , 幾乎不太一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不能立即生存 , 語言會分崩離析 , 試圖描述在其中一個噴射流中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這就有點像經歷一次超新星的爆炸 , 但在瞬間的距離又會是數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那噴射流是在如此精確地發生之後的數十億年後在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述、模型、預測、並解釋 , 在所有東西的另一端 , 顯示了現實中所發生的 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個類星體的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是表面的圖像 , 雖然也包含了解釋性的模型 , 將同樣的數學關係和因果結構體現出來 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 那麼這個結構與另一個相似之處在於時間的增長 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那樣的實體物體 , 不像彼此可能是一樣的 , 不論如何 , 都能體現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 且隨著時間越來越長 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性的存在 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構含有不斷增加的精確性 , 每樣東西的結構 。 這個地方 , 以及宇宙中其他地方 , 都是包含在內的結構性和因果關係中的精髓 。 所以 , 離物理定律很遙遠 , 物理定律允許這一切發生 , 甚至指出這可能發生的 , 是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們的形式是如何獲取這個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的一個觀點是真的 , 這是真的 , 但這是錯的 。 有一點是正確的 。 就是它沒有特殊的物理特徵 , 沒有任何奇蹟牽涉其中 。 它只會用三種而已 。 它是錯誤的 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種信息處理的形式 。 信息處理的形式是計算 , 計算需要一種電腦--沒有物質可以製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 較不明顯 , 但對於開放式的知識和解釋 , 也是必要的 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好轉向測試 , 舉例來說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律大約在三百年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們習以為常的證據 , 早在那之前的每平方公尺就跌在地球上數十億年 , 之後的數十億年就繼續墜落 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本的真理的證據就在我們的星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點飽和證據 , 同時也充滿物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的先決條件 , 是他們最低的可供性 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它空無一物 , 非常寒冷 , 那裡一片漆黑 , 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹義的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一下 , 在星系間空間中的一個立方體 , 和我們的家園一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體非常空 , 依然代表著它含有超過百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造 , 例如一個自給自足的太空站 , 裡面有一群科學家 , 致力於創造開放式的知識 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西並非物理定律所禁止的 , 那麼 , 除了知道如何運作之外 , 還有什麼可能阻礙我們去做呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能夠做到 , 我們將自動提供能源 , 因為轉變將是核融合反應爐和證據呢 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣地 , 那裡也暗得住人 。 但你所要做的只是拿個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這裡看到同樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	再加上一個更強大的望遠鏡你將可以看見恆星和行星
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將可以進行天體物理學研究 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地你可以製造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等.
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	也許最難做得科學研究是生物學實地考察因為要到好幾億年才能到達最近的有生命的星球再回來
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來沒有那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔數億年就做一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了所有開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個角落 , 都可以成為我們這種中心 , 只要知道如何做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不在獨特的友善環境裡 ,
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境也是一樣 。 地球也是一樣 。 所以一個受污染的地球也是一樣 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 那裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙知識為基礎的觀點我認為應該要讓我們感到非常特別 。 但這也應該要讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意謂著 , 若沒有所需的特定知識 , 能在宇宙中繼續存活下去的挑戰中存活下去 , 我們將無法存活下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年外的超新星 , 我們就死定了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近寫了一本關於我們人類對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出了差錯 , 最重要的是用大規模殺傷性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活在這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚些時候會在大會上講到這個
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我認為 , 可能性不適合在這個議題上討論 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我的確同意他的看法 。 我們可以生存下來 , 而且我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機會 , 而是我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是史無前例的 。 物種常常會滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明會結束 。 絕大多數的物種和所有曾經存在過的文明都是現在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 那麼邏輯上來說 , 我們唯一的希望是利用區別我們物種的這個特徵以及我們的文明--也就是說 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以現在讓我把這套用在當前的爭議 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議就是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但我不是對的物理學家 。 根據全球暖化 , 我只是個懶漢 。 要說真的 , 科學理論是普遍存在的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 避免大災難已經太晚了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們現在最好的選擇是用像是京都議定書之類的措施來預防二氧化碳排放 , 限制經濟活動 , 花費數千億美元之類的措施 , 那麼 , 任何合理的措施 , 這就已經是個災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被提倡的舉動甚至不用花心力去解決問題 , 只需要稍微延遲一下就行了 。 所以避免此事已經太晚了 , 本來可能又太晚才有人意識到這危險 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	很可能在1970年代就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將預估新的冰河時期會有數十億人死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這當中的教訓對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有在公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們不可能永遠知道的 。 當我們知道一場即將發生的災難 , 以及如何用比災難本身還少的成本來解決 , 那麼將不會有太多的爭論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們還未能預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要加以解決問題 , 而不是僅僅加以解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一磅的療法 , 但只有這樣 , 我們才能知道預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經對著鼻子被打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學就不是教你如何避開拳頭的 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療 , 只專注在預防 , 那麼它也只能做到很少 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界正在緩和氣體排放 , 計畫不計成本降低氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要配合降低溫度的計畫 , 規劃在更高溫狀態下生活的計畫 , 不計成本 , 而是有效且廉價的 。 有些計畫存在 , 比如在太空中大量的鏡子 , 會將陽光轉向 , 鼓勵水生生物多吃點二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們並非人類努力去面對這個問題的核心 , 也不是大體上的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	至於我們還沒有意識到的問題 , 能正確解決的能力--不是無限期的好運--是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 更是為生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	把兩塊石板雕刻在上面
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而另一塊刻上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何能脫離貧窮 , 如果它是惡劣規則的體制 ? 經濟學家保羅羅•羅莫揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區 」 、 「 城市規劃 」 、 「 城市規範區 」 , 被一個國家的聯盟所管理 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅•羅默的激進想法:特區市
take a look at this picture .	看一下這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我碰過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子吧 , 穿綠衣的那個
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	咱們也來給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森也有支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以謎題來了:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森有尖端科技 , 例如手機 , 但卻沒有辦法在家裡發電 , 使用100年的技術 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡而言之 , 答案就是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的制度可以預防雙贏辦法的產生當人們可以把新科技帶進像尼爾森這樣的人手上
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則呢 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵守規則 , 說明它必須以極低、補貼的價格銷售 , 事實上 , 價格非常低 , 以至於每賣出一個電力 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵 , 來接上其他許多使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到了 , 有一套不同的規則 , 讓企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以 , 他們有動機讓更多客戶參加 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	尼爾森收購電信的手機公司就是用這樣的規則在運作 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過這些規則如何運作良好
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價制度的制度 , 但他卻遇到了來自企業及消費者的抗議 , 他們想要保存既有的補助制度 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入了一些規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏辦法來幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而尼爾森則卡在路燈下讀書
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	那時候真正的挑戰 , 是試著找出我們該如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們是否可以發展出一些規則來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 我們可以有一個普遍的抽象概念 , 那就是 , 如果我們可以給人們更多的選擇 , 和更多的選擇 , 對很多國家的領袖而言 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 要把兩者之間的反對呈現出來是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者的那種選擇 , 例如給總統提高電價的選擇 , 帶走一個經濟人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠繼續享有補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只提供一方或者另一方你會有張力或摩擦力
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那將給我們一系列改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路可使用 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想看到規則所帶來的破壞性效應那些規則可以使人在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜間拍攝的照片
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	拉近一點看這裡 , 你可以看到北韓這塊跟它的鄰國比起來就像是個黑洞
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在你不會驚訝於北韓的規則使人們一直保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 我們要認識到北韓和南韓開始時用的是同一套制度 , 既有法律和規範 , 也要用在更深層的層面上 , 了解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 以及信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離出來時 , 他們做了一些選擇 , 導致了非常歧異的路徑 , 用於他們的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變身為人類 , 可以改變彼此互動的規則 , 不論是好是壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地這裡 , 放大這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗與它的鄰居多明尼加相比 , 它的居民人數也差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各的黑暗 , 有一半的居民是海地 , 或是多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是體制之所以不良是因為政府的軟弱
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不單單是因為政府太強壯、太有壓迫性了 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有良好體制的環境 , 我們就不能只是拆掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得想辦法建立起來 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地向我們展示了與規則合作的潛力與挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這個圖表的一開始 , 中國是全球高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人擁有先驅性的科技像是鋼鐵、印刷、火藥
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則會促使那些想法散播出去 , 這個利益的動機原本可以促使傳播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 把創新能力放慢 , 讓中國與世界隔絕 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 中國也在發展新制度時 , 被那些進步給削減了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入停滯不前 , 因為它在世界其他地方拉扯 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國的平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代時你們可以看到這個數字大約是3%
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國經濟開始起飛中國人開始趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖 , 你就能得到線索 , 來引領中國體制的巨大改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的這點 , 各位可以在輪廓邊上看到 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國的一小部份在20世紀大部分的時間 , 都是在非常不同的體制下運作的 , 與中國其他的大陸的規則是仿效當時的勞動市場經濟 , 並由英國人來負責 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸 , 開始做像縫紉做的工作 , 做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了要踏上增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致那裡的成長非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範本是讓像鄧小平這樣的領導者可以複製的當他們決定將整個大陸推向市場模式時
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個中國人立即轉移市場模式 , 不如從設立一些特區著手進行 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的:讓有機會與市場規則合作 , 讓想參與其中的人有機會實現市場規則 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以 , 他們在香港周圍建了四個經濟特區:中國人可以來這裡工作的地區 , 城市迅速在那兒成長 ; 外國企業也能進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一座城市-深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡有台灣企業製作的iphone你們當中許多人都擁有它而他們將它與中國人搬到深圳打工
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿海城市以同樣的觀點在開放 , 最終 , 在這些人們可以選擇去的地方 , 展現出成功 , 因為他們提供的優勢 , 所以他們會聚集在一起 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	示範成功 , 促成了整個經濟體的共識朝向市場模式邁進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示了好幾個重點
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:保留人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模適用
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試圖改變一個村落的體制 , 你可以這麼做 , 但是一個村莊實在太小了 , 無法得到那種好處 , 如果你有幾百萬人在好的體制下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試圖改變國內的規則 , 你就無法給一些人一個機會去壓制 , 看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但都市能給你這個機會去創造新的地方 , 用新的規則 , 讓大家可以參與其中 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大了 , 足以將我們所有人在好規則下工作時所能得到的好處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以這個提議就是我們構想的一個叫做 " 特區市 "
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個憲章開始 , 規定了建造城市所需要的所有規則 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們會需要吸引投資者來建造基礎建設電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引企業 , 他們會先到那兒去找搬走的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	然後你會需要吸引家家戶戶戶們來永久居住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 然後獲得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	這個城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們就可以把這個模型的規模做大 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍的進行
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它成功 , 我們需要很好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些被記錄在憲章中 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這已經成為一個模式如果我們允許在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領土開始
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新憲章之下 , 但沒有人會被迫在它之下生活 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導者所需要的選擇我們必須允許國家之間的可行性合作的可能性事實上 , 中國和英國的合作方式首先是小小的市場模式然後再擴展到整個中國
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地透過香港的行動 , 來減少世界貧窮的影響 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫的數量還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作再複製這種模式 , 我們就能得到擴展到全世界的各種利益 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的刪除 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的控制權 , 來掌控特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這麼說時 , 在座有些人開始會想: 「 嗯 , 這只會帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但很重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生出來的情緒會阻礙我們 , 讓我們退開 , 關掉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方 , 和我們的一些援助計畫中 , 剩下的只是強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式的重點就是選擇 , 無論是對領袖 , 還是那些將會居住在這些新地方的人民 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 " 選擇 " 正是強制和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談 , 這要如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們拿一位特別的領導人 , raulcastro , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有想過他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的事 , 但他在古巴的小島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方一點光線 , 有著很特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一區政府提供美國行政負責一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大的總理對他說: 「 看 , 雅肯族的問題很糟 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你們加拿大何不接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立特別的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	在那裡建造一座新城市 。
allow many people to come in .	允許許多多的人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有隻香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人則等著拿回來 。 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結起來的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模式還可以在哪裡試行呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們中的許多人完全可以理解特區這個概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為一條規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人民意見而不受強制性 , 以及強制性的反對勢力 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有可信的承諾 , 那些願意建港口、修建道路的投資者 , 在新的城市中 , 他們可以做出更有可信的承諾 , 如果他們能與夥伴國家合作的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至是一些安排有點像信託管理帳戶你把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡然後交由合夥國家來負責
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以用來建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣一大片延伸出去的土地上 , 有數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納並思考 , 不僅僅是一、二個特區市而是數十個替數億人創造地方的城市 , 也許下個世紀就會有數十億人移居到城市去 , 他們是否有足夠的土地容納他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們看看夜晚的燈光 , 有一件事是會誤導的 , 就是說 , 在視覺上 , 看起來世界上大部分的地區都已經是用視覺來建造的 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來告訴你們為什麼這樣做是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把所有的土地都呈現出來 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個正方形代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被現在居住的城市30億人所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到這個長方形的底部你會發現這些30億居民的城市只佔了地球上3%的可耕地
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要再為十億人建造城市 , 他們會變成像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從3%的可耕地走到4%
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們通過建造更多城市 , 來大幅降低人類在地球上的足跡 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市以良好的規則為治理 , 它們可以成為一個城市 , 在那些城市中 , 人們受到犯罪、疾病和衛生不良、人們有機會找工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到像電力這種基本公共設施 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一座特區城市 , 擴展規模 , 需要什麼 ?
it would help to have a manual .	使用說明會很有幫助 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的就是寫一些細節可以放進這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理這些城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外出櫃 ,
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但你可以讓我們開始思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設不只加拿大和拉爾卡斯楚之間的交易有關 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	巴西也來參一腳西班牙 。 或許古巴想成為四方合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定協定 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這沒什麼先例可是很容易成功
how would we finance this ?	我們要怎麼資助這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是他們一開始所擁有土地的土地價值大大增的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值來支付如警察、法院等物資的收入 , 但是學校體系和醫療體系 , 這使得這個地方變得更吸引人居住 , 使得人們有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 那些有助於建構這塊區域並建立起基本規則的人 , 會走對的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有許多其它類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們怎麼可能讓那些一開始工作的人們能用低成本且負擔得起的建築物 , 比如iphone , 但讓那些建築能節能 , 且確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會落在地震或颶風的環境中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節尚待解決 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些東西的人 , 已經可以看出沒有路障 , 除了缺乏想像力之外 , 還可以讓我們無法實現真正的全球性的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做個總結
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能這麼幸福 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以跟別人分享想法當他們發現時跟我們分享
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有的物品 , 在那裡 , 分享意味著我們得到的愈來愈少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但有另一類想法:主宰我們互動的規則像是 , 咱們來訂個賦稅制度 , 來支援一所研究型大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個制度 , 我們擁有土地擁有在政府辦公室註冊的權利 , 人民可以承擔作為附屬品 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能持續創新在規則上尤其是創新在改變規則上我們就不會卡在不良的規則上而真正地讓世界變得更好讓尼爾森和他的朋友再也不用在街燈下讀書了 。 謝謝
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	先驅克萊格•凡特從史詩般的圓形探險中休息一下 , 來談談他的團隊到目前為止已經在探索海洋生物多樣性的數百萬個基因 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明海洋、科學、科技
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特對dna和海洋的影響 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 有幾個人問我關於衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將是我對它的唯一評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者非常勝過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在這18分鐘內要告訴你們的是我們要如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換到最初階段開始自己編寫基因編碼
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前的這個月我們發表了第一組免費有機體的基因序列也就是流感的嗜血桿菌
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這項基因組計畫從十三年降到四個月
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同一個基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年裡 , 大量的基因組被加進去:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、昆蟲和幾種哺乳類動物 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前 , 基因組學的這個階段是在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五組基因組的測序 ; 它已經進行數百組的測序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得一項補助 , 今年我們以環保組織為中心的一個側寫計畫來排序130組基因組 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 當我們去看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到在這星球上有什麼可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人都沒有意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球上生物總量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔了所有生物總量的千分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津的居民經常做的事 , 但如果你曾經去過海邊 , 吞一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬隻細菌 , 且以一千萬隻病毒為單位 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	到兩年前 , 只有少於5 , 000種微生物被特徵 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們啟動了 「 足球三號 」 探險 , 我們每隔200英里就要進行一次遠征 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始我們的試驗計劃 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東海岸工作 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 現在我們正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上進行此項任務 , 有一部分是為了刺激年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要取得海水並過濾它 , 然後在不同的濾鏡上收集不同大小的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡我們可以每24小時完成一億個字母的基因編碼的測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這麼做 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 一般認為我們眼中的視覺色素在這個環境中只有一兩種有機體擁有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界暖化地區的上半部海洋中的每一種物種 , 都有相同的感光細胞 , 並以陽光作為它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新基因 , 和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這個計畫延伸到空氣上 , 利用史隆基金的資助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量 , 我們所有人每天所呼吸的病毒和細菌數量 , 特別是在飛機上或密閉的禮堂裡 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 僅僅一天之內 , 我們從紐約市的一棟大樓上 , 收集十億微生物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正在測序這一切 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	單單是從資料收集這一面 , 就在我們穿過加拉巴哥群島的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每隔200英里 , 我們在大海樣本中會看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些理由完全合理 , 用不同的溫度梯度來說 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張以溫度為基礎的衛星照片--紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是溫暖的--而我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本中有極大的差異 , 就充足的物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一個讓我們相當驚訝的是這些光感接收器會感應不同波長的光線 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些變化多端 , 從地區到地區 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外 , 在幾乎是藍色的深海中 , 感光受體會看見藍色光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化更大可能是朝著極端的紅外線和紫外線前進
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了試圖評估我們的基因庫是什麼 , 我們集合了所有的資料 , 包括我們遠征時全部的資料 , 代表地球上一半以上的基因資料 , 總計大約有兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果我們發現我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但每一種我們從環境中取得的新樣本都以線性的方式增加 , 為這些新家庭提供線性樣本 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處於早期發現的階段 , 關於基本基因、構成以及地球上生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角與動物同在 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約有2千9百萬組基因 , 我們的基因組當中只有大約2萬4千組 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果把所有動物的基因組合起來 , 我們所共有的基因族群大概只有三萬不到一點 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因並不是現在才有進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們從基因中心論來看-或許回到了理查•道金斯的想法而不是以基因為中心的觀點來解釋這些基因組成分成的不同構造
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力在過去二十年中已經發生了變化現在dna測序的速度非常快又便宜
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	關於合成基因組學我們首次想到1995年我們完成第二組基因組定序那從mycoplasma生殖器官定序
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤衫上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但有大約500對基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800對基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們很簡單的問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800個、500個 , 是否有一組基因 , 可能構成一個最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因編碼的小段的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果插入到基因的正中間 , 會阻斷其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有所有可以採取轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對這個非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中必要或非必要的基因來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著更直接地用13種有關生物體的基因組來做研究 , 我們試著比較以上全部 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	然後我們得到這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173種基因存在於所有13種生物中 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽視一種細胞寄生蟲 , 池塘會稍微擴大一點 , 當我們觀察核心基因組 , 大約310組 , 它會擴展得更多 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以根據你的觀點 , 擴大或是收縮基因組 , 到500個最少的300到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些點子的唯一方法就是用那些基因建構出一條人造染色體 , 我們必須以一個模塊式的方式來進行 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大型片斷中合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 在這上面是我的同事 , 開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內製造一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 精確度達到100% , 就它的序列和生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人振奮的實驗當我們把合成的dna注入到細菌中 , 突然間 , 那dna就開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 一轉又一轉 , 然後殺死了細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是合成病毒的第一個年頭--小兒麻痺病毒--但是它的活性只有原先的萬分之一--花了三年的時間
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174結構的漫畫
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體能打造自身硬體的案例 , 那就是我們對於生物學的認識 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們會立刻開始關心生物戰 , 我最近在參議院委員會舉行的證詞 , 以及美國政府設立的一個專門委員會來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	而我認為 , 把現實記在心裡是很重要的 , 與人們的想像力比較 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成測序的病毒基因組都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會立即對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐萬分 , 但來自這種病源體的dna並不是可行的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造了天花的基因組 , 那dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓國安部門擔憂的是設計病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 致力於創立生物武器代理工會 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那些研究真的被打斷了 , 那將來在製造設計病毒上就應該只有很少的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞生物
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能也就是我們所擁有的真核細胞在十年內就可能發生的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在要做出數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這些放入人造染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 該如何把所有其他的
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片斷開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將這些片斷組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體上衍生出來的 , 耐輻射奇異球菌 , 它能承受三百萬拉德輻射量 , 且不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它在輻射爆炸12至24小時後重新組合它的基因體 , 在它的染色體被完全分解後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在也許由於我們在外太空的旅行
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是經過約50萬拉德輻射照射過後的玻璃瓶 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒裂開 , 微生物的底部變得更開心也更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的照片:上面這張圖顯示的是經過一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全炸開 ,
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這裡有同樣的dna在24小時後自動重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這些生物能夠做到 , 真的很震驚 , 我們這個星球上可能就有上千種不同的物種 , 它們能做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合之後 , 第一步只是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅可以了解生物學的基礎 , 同時也可以也可以了解環境和社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	比如 , 從我們所測序的第三個生物上 , 甲烷ocococcusjannaschii它生存在沸騰的水溫當中 , 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它所有的碳都來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 如今上千種不同的生物都以二氧化碳為生 , 並且能將之捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油中取得碳來做合成 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 並從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 將之轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物是依靠一氧化碳而存活的 , 我們用它作為一種降低效能的生物 , 來分解水 , 以產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數條路徑 , 可以被改造成代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一項重大的項目 , 該項目與挪威的石油取得並將甲烷從天然氣場轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我認為將會有一個全新的領域出現 , 叫做 「 組合基因學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可以製造或許百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就像所有生物一樣 , 通過篩選 , 無論是用氫氣製成 , 或是化學製品 , 或僅僅是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的作用 , 會在接觸範圍內很好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用的過程從陽光直接產生氫氣
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的氫化酶將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維素 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖類的酵素在同一個細胞中發酵 , 以產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在使用微生物的主要實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中最好的化合物所產生的化學指數比我們最好的化學家所能產出的更為複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來工程的物種可以成為食物的來源 , 希望能成為能源、環境的補救措施 , 或許還能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與了這個活動
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都把他們的經文拿來當法律書 , 他們找不到任何關於禁止製造生命的資訊 , 所以這方面就沒關係了 。 最終的疑慮是生物戰的面向 , 但卻給了我們打算開始做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前史隆基金會為此剛剛資助了一個多機構的研究項目 , 找出這方面的風險和益處 , 以及像我一樣的科學團隊所應該使用的規則 , 在這個領域中 , 我們試著設置好的例子 , 隨著前進 ,
these are complex issues .	這些複雜的議題
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 也許能徹底改變開發中國家能做的事 , 並透過各種簡單的過程來提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說過 , 快樂與成功根植在絕大多數人不認同的特質上:我們引導過去、現在和未來的方式 。 他建議我們按照時間來調整我們的觀點 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦津巴多開的藥方很健康 , 準時到位 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享時間的秘密力量在很短的時間內
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	視頻:好了 , 開始計時 。 30秒--工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 請坐下 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大概就是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個吧 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來調查校長在亞當的誘惑之中的對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 拜託亞當 , 別這麼想 , 咬一口吧 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	" 一口 , 亞當.不要放棄伊娃. "
" i don't know , guys .	" 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	" 好吧 。 一口 , 搞什麼鬼 ? "
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生活是誘惑 。 重點是要量產 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 稍後 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在 , 焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會因為當下的熱情而落入獵物 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚前保持貞操的少女中 , 感謝小布施-大多數 , 約有60% , 要在一年內獲得性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有使用節育 。
so much for promises .	以至於我們承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們來試試四歲的孩子 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖了 。 但是如果他們等到實驗員回來時 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然是要付出代價的 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖的話 , 還要等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的是三分之二的孩子們給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等.其他人當然要等.
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延後了現在 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 十四年後回到那兒 , 試圖發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多層面上 , 孩子與孩子之間有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抗拒在sat上的得分高出250分的孩子
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 。 這就像一整組不同智商的點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們並沒有惹上那麼多麻煩 。 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們自信、堅定不移 。 而對我來說 , 今天的關鍵是 , 他們是以未來為焦點 , 而不是以未來為焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間透視法就是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類經歷的流動劃分為不同的時間區域或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你自動或無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們在文化、國家之間、個人間、社會階級之間、教育程度不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	而問題在於他們可能會變得偏頗 , 因為你學會了過度使用他們一些而低估其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你所做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對一些人而言 , 只關於當下情況 , 別人在做什麼 , 和你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	當這些人以這種形式做決定時 , 我們就叫他們 「 處於現實生活 」 , 因為他們所關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是無關緊要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去的經歷是怎樣的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的記憶
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們要稱那些人為 " 懷舊主義 " , 因為他們關注的是過去式 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對於另一些人 , 不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在於預期結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 " 以未來為目的 " 。 他們的重點是 「 將來會怎樣 」 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間觀點的悖論 , 是它會影響你做的每一個決策 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有偏見的時間範圍 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實他們有六種方式 。 有兩種方式可以當作 「 現代化 」 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被 " 懷舊主義 " , 兩種方式成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把注意力放在 " 正面懷舊 " 或 " 負面懷舊 " .
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 「 享受主義者 」 , 即你專注於人生的喜悅 , 或 「 當代主義者 」 這並不重要 , 你的生命被控制住 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 " 理想主義 " , 設定目標
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 死後生命開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 以轉換時間觀點 , 根據情況的需求而有流利 , 這才是你要學的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度在未來
and moderate on presenthedonism .	調整到當下主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	並且永遠地低估了消極和不合法的存在 。
